implements `SetupSignalContext()` and `SetupSignalHandler()` functions that register for SIGTERM and SIGINT signals\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go` defines `shutdownSignals = []os.Signal{os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM}`\\n- The signal handlers use `signal.Notify()` to register with a buffered channel (capacity 2) to capture up to two signals\\n- A context is created with `context.WithCancel()` that gets cancelled on the first signal\\n- On the second signal, the program exits immediately with `os.Exit(1)`, allowing forceful termination if graceful shutdown hangs\\n\\n**Graceful Shutdown Pattern:**\\n- The implementation uses context cancellation as the shutdown mechanism\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/kms/internal/plugins/_mock/plugin.go` demonstrates the pattern with `withShutdownSignal()` that wraps context and returns a cancellable context\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/kms/pkg/service/grpc_service.go` calls `GracefulStop()` on the gRPC server when context is done\\n\\n**Cleanup Ordering:**\\n- When shutdown signal is received, context is cancelled which triggers cleanup in dependent services\\n- The two-signal approach ensures: first signal initiates graceful shutdown, second signal forces immediate exit\\n\\n### grafana/grafana\\n\\n**Signal Handler Registration:**\\n- `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` implements `listenToSystemSignals()` that registers for SIGTERM, SIGINT (via os.Interrupt), and SIGHUP signals\\n- Uses separate channels for SIGHUP and SIGTERM/SIGINT to handle reload separately from shutdown\\n- Signal handlers run in an infinite loop checking both signal channels\\n\\n**Graceful Shutdown Pattern:**\\n- On SIGTERM/SIGINT, creates a context with 30-second timeout: `context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)`\\n- Calls `s.Shutdown(ctx, ...)` with the timeout context\\n- `pkg/server/server.go` Shutdown method:\\n  - Uses `sync.Once` to ensure shutdown only happens once\\n  - Calls `managerAdapter.Shutdown()` to shutdown background services\\n  - Waits on context with a select statement\\n- `pkg/services/grpcserver/service.go` shutdown method:\\n  - Calls `s.server.GracefulStop()` in a goroutine\\n  - Has explicit timeout handling with `time.After(s.cfg.GracefulShutdownTimeout)`\\n  - If graceful stop completes in time, logs success; if timeout occurs, calls `Stop()` to force shutdown\\n  - Configuration timeout is defined in `pkg/setting/setting_grpc.go` with default 10 seconds\\n\\n**Cleanup Ordering:**\\n- gRPC server drains connections first via `GracefulStop()` before forcing stop\\n- Background services shut down before gRPC server\\n- 30-second overall shutdown timeout ensures bounded shutdown time\\n\\n**Multiple Signal Handlers:**\\n- Operators in `pkg/operators/provisioning/` and `pkg/operators/iam/` each register their own signal handlers\\n- Each creates a context and cancels it on SIGTERM/SIGINT signal\\n\\n### prometheus/prometheus\\n\\n**Signal Handler Registration:**\\n- `cmd/prometheus/main.go` uses `oklog/run` library for service orchestration\\n- Creates a channel `term := make(chan os.Signal, 1)` and registers: `signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)`\\n- Signal is received via the run group's executor pattern\\n\\n**Graceful Shutdown Pattern:**\\n- Uses `oklog/run` Group to manage multiple services with coordinated shutdown\\n- When SIGTERM/SIGINT is received, the signal triggers the group's interrupt function which calls Stop() on all services\\n- Services are stopped in reverse order of registration\\n\\n**Drain on Shutdown:**\\n- `notifier/manager.go` defines `Options` struct with `DrainOnShutdown bool` field\\n- `notifier/sendloop.go` implements the drain pattern:\\n  - `stop()` method checks if `DrainOnShutdown` is true\\n  - If true, calls `drainQueue()` which processes all pending alerts before returning\\n  - If false, logs warning and counts dropped alerts\\n  - `drainQueue()` loops through queue calling `sendOneBatch()` until queue is empty\\n- Configuration flag `--alertmanager.drain-notification-queue-on-shutdown` (default true) controls this behavior\\n- `notifier/manager.go` Run method returns only after all pending notifications are drained\\n\\n**Cleanup Ordering:**\\n- Discovery managers stop first (notification and scrape)\\n- Notifier manager stops with queue draining\\n- Rule manager stops\\n- Web handler stops\\n- Each service's Stop() function is called in reverse order, allowing earlier services to drain while later services are still active\\n\\n### Common Patterns\\n\\n1. **Signal Registration:** All three use `os/signal.Notify()` with buffered channels\\n2. **Multi-Signal Handling:** Support for second signal to force exit (Kubernetes explicitly, others via framework)\\n3. **Graceful Shutdown Mechanism:** \\n   - Kubernetes: Context cancellation\\n   - Grafana: Explicit shutdown methods with timeout context\\n   - Prometheus: Service group orchestration with drain functionality\\n4. **Timeout Protection:** Bounded shutdown time prevents indefinite hangs\\n   - Kubernetes: Second signal forces exit\\n   - Grafana: Explicit 30-second timeout (or service-specific like 10s for gRPC)\\n   - Prometheus: Service dependencies ensure cleanup completes or forces stop\\n5. **Drain Before Stop:** Important for notification/alert systems to avoid losing data\\n\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2028,"cache_read_input_tokens":80737,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2028},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"0957dd38-afc7-4713-9fca-dbbca32b80b9","uuid":"1825971e-0f5d-401c-bb7c-ac9e2d834dac"}
